Like we learned in writing about his brief minor-league career, Thomas wasn’t short on confidence, even though -- or because -- he felt like evaluators overlooked him.\n* Cooperstown or Canton for Frank Thomas? - chicagotribune.com\n* Frank Thomas: From Auburn tight end to Cooperstown - AuburnTigers.com\n* Frank Thomas remembers Auburn on way to Hall of Fame - AuburnTigers.com\nLook back far enough into Thomas’ career, and you’ll start talking about his football career at Auburn. Here we find ourselves with some conflicting information. Thomas says football coach Pat Dye said he should pursue baseball; Thomas recalls Dye saying, “I think you’ll be a very, very good football player, but you’re not going to be that level that you are in baseball.”\nBut Dye now tells the school’s site, “If he had stuck with football, he’d be going in the Hall of Fame as a football player.”\nEither Dye is being polite, or he misspoke and the Sox gained. Either way, Paul Sullivan talked to Mike Rizzo, the scout who signed Thomas. Thomas’ agent tried selling football as an alternate career, and Rizzo didn’t buy it.\n* Stats obsession helped push Frank Thomas to great heights - Chicago Sun-Times\n* Paul Konerko lauds Frank Thomas for being ‘dialed in with his work’ - Chicago Sun-Times\nTime heals all wounds, not just between Thomas and the Sox, but between Thomas and the people -- media and teammates, mainly -- who thought Thomas paid too much attention to his stats, because they realize that it’s all just motivation. And hell, if my baseball card looked like Thomas’, I’d want to know what my numbers were at all times, too.\n* Frank Thomas is Hall of Famer because of great batting eye | HardballTalk\nJoe Posnanski knows that good players’ good stats are good for the team, and so he raves about Thomas’ legendary eye. These two paragraphs are plenty of fun:\n* No place for steroid users in the Hall of Fame - chicagotribune.com\n* Big Hurt stressed, grateful as induction nears | whitesox.com: News\nEven if Thomas wanted to spend his Hall of Fame speech lambasting steroid users, it would probably sound redundant after answering all the questions about it over various media sessions dating back to January. Good news -- Thomas said he’s reserving his speech to thank the people along the way who made his career possible. data-concert="desktop_leaderboard_variable"></div></div><article><div class="duet--article--lede duet--page-layout--standard-article"><div class="duet--ledes--standard-lede _17edt8c0 _1nfb3k43"><div class="_17edt8c1"><div class="_1tww7100"><div class="_1tww7103"><span class="_13l11za17"><ul class="_153sp3oe"><li class=""><a href="/chicago-white-sox-news" class="_153sp3o2 ls9zuh6 ls9zuh5">Chicago White Sox News</a></li></ul></span></div><div class=""><h1 class="_1jeon7i1 _1jeon7i0 _1jeon7i6 ls9zuha ls9zuh9">Reading Room: All about Frank Thomas</h1><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup _1jeon7ih _1jeon7ig ls9zuha">Waiting to see The Big Hurt enter the Hall of Fame? Bide your time with a ton of articles</p></div></div></div><div class=""><div class="_17edt8c3"><div class="_13l11za1 _13l11za0"><div class="_13l11za9 _13l11zai"><div class="duet--article--article-byline ls9zuha ayeadi0"><span class=""><span>by</span> <!-- --> <span class="ayeadi2 ayeadi3"><a href="/authors/jim-margalus">Jim Margalus</a></span></span></div><span class="duet--article--timestamp gq1ypc4 gq1ypc1 gq1ypc0 ls9zuh5 ls9zuha"><time dateTime="2014-07-27T10:00:02+00:00">Jul 27, 2014, 10:00 AM UTC</time></span></div><div class="_13l11zan _13l11zam _13l11zau _13l11zaw"><div class="_13l11zay _13l11zax"><span class="_13l11za17"><ul class="duet--article--share-buttons ty756p0"><li><button aria-label="Share on Facebook" class="ty756p1"><svg class="ty756pc" width="40" height="40" viewBox="0 0 40 40" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><title>Facebook</title><path d="M27.0174 21.7497L27.8495 16.3604H22.6403V12.8637C22.6403 11.3906 23.3668 9.95151 25.7019 9.95151H28.0714V5.36435C28.0714 5.36435 25.9212 5 23.866 5C19.5761 5 16.7707 7.57929 16.7707 12.2529V16.3604H12V21.7497H16.7707V34.7746C17.727 34.924 18.707 35 19.7055 35C20.704 35 21.6841 34.9214 22.6403 34.7746V21.7497H27.0174Z" fill=""></path></svg></button></li><li><div class="ty756po"><button aria-label="Copy link" class="ty756p1"><svg class="ty756pc" width="40" height="40" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 40 40" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><title>Link</title><path d="M16.9691 32.9499C14.2358 35.6832 9.78321 35.6832 7.04996 32.9499C4.31671 30.2166 4.31665 25.764 7.04996 23.0307L12.5606 17.52C15.294 14.7867 19.7465 14.7867 22.4798 17.52C22.704 17.7383 22.8315 18.037 22.8337 18.3499C22.8359 18.6628 22.7125 18.9634 22.4912 19.1846C22.2702 19.4059 21.9693 19.5293 21.6568 19.5271C21.3439 19.5249 21.0449 19.3975 20.8266 19.1732C18.9805 17.3271 16.0599 17.3271 14.2137 19.1732L8.70306 24.6839C6.85694 26.53 6.85694 29.4507 8.70306 31.2968C10.5492 33.1429 13.4698 33.1426 15.3159 31.2968L20.551 26.0614V26.0617C20.7693 25.8375 21.0683 25.71 21.3811 25.7078C21.694 25.7056 21.9946 25.829 22.2159 26.0503C22.4368 26.2716 22.5602 26.5722 22.5581 26.885C22.5559 27.1979 22.4284 27.4966 22.2042 27.7149L16.9691 32.9499ZM27.4394 22.4796C24.706 25.2129 20.2535 25.2129 17.5202 22.4796V22.4799C17.296 22.2616 17.1685 21.9629 17.1663 21.65C17.1644 21.3372 17.2875 21.0366 17.5088 20.8153C17.7301 20.5941 18.0307 20.4707 18.3435 20.4728C18.6564 20.475 18.9551 20.6025 19.1734 20.8267C21.0195 22.6728 23.9401 22.6728 25.7863 20.8267L31.2969 15.316C33.1431 13.4699 33.1431 10.5493 31.2969 8.70316C29.4508 6.85704 26.5302 6.85704 24.6841 8.70316L19.449 13.9382C19.2307 14.1625 18.9317 14.2902 18.6189 14.2924C18.306 14.2946 18.0054 14.1712 17.7841 13.9499C17.5629 13.7286 17.4395 13.428 17.4417 13.1149C17.4438 12.802 17.5713 12.503 17.7958 12.285L23.0309 7.04999C25.7642 4.31667 30.2168 4.31667 32.95 7.04999C35.6833 9.7833 35.6834 14.2359 32.95 16.9691L27.4394 22.4798L27.4394 22.4796Z"></path></svg></button></div></li></ul></span></div></div><div class="_13l11za19"><div class="_1joyojp8 _1joyojp0 _1joyojp2b"><div class="_1joyojp0 _1joyojpf _1joyojp9" data-concert="article_sponsorship_mobile_and_tablet"></div></div></div><div class="_13l11za1r _13l11za1y"><div class="_13l11za1h"><div class="_1joyojp8 _1joyojp0 _1joyojp2c"><div class="_1joyojp0 _1joyojp9" data-concert="article_sponsorship_desktop"></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="duet--layout--entry-body-container _19a1t550 _1nfb3k43 _1nfb3k413"><div class="_19a1t551"><div class="duet--layout--entry-body lcwall0"><div class="duet--ledes--standard-lede-bottom"><div class="_1u9wjr40 _1nfb3k4e"><div class="stn-video-player" data-stn-player="hjktaqhy" data-s2n-api="setupS2NApi"></div><div class="sticky-nav-trigger"></div></div></div><div id="zephr-anchor" class="_1nfb3k410"><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><div class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup _458ieq0"><p>Today is the day that's been 25 years in the making -- <a class="sbn-auto-link" href="http://www.sbnation.com/mlb/players/865/frank-thomas">Frank Thomas</a>' Hall of Fame induction. He's receiving warranted attention on the eve of the ceremony, and so this Reading Room is all for him.</p></div></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><ul class="duet--article--unordered-list _1nfb3k4i feuejx0 ls9zuh1"><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.baseballamerica.com/majors/hall-of-fame-frank-thomas-pushed-doubts-slights/">Hall Of Fame Commemorative: Thomas Pushed By Doubts, Slights - BaseballAmerica.com</a></span></li></ul></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">Since Frank Thomas was Baseball America’s Minor League Player of the Year in 1989, the magazine republished its story on him from that season. Like we learned in writing about his brief minor-league career, Thomas wasn’t short on confidence, even though -- or because -- he felt like evaluators overlooked him.</p></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><ul class="duet--article--unordered-list _1nfb3k4i feuejx0 ls9zuh1"><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.chicagotribune.com/sports/baseball/whitesox/ct-frank-thomas-auburn-hall-of-fame-spt-0726-hall--20140726,0,6352268.story?track=rss">Cooperstown or Canton for Frank Thomas? - chicagotribune.com</a></span></li><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.auburntigers.com/sports/m-basebl/spec-rel/072314aaa.html">Frank Thomas: From Auburn tight end to Cooperstown - AuburnTigers.com</a></span></li><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.auburntigers.com/sports/m-footbl/spec-rel/072614aaa.html">Frank Thomas remembers Auburn on way to Hall of Fame - AuburnTigers.com</a></span></li></ul></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">Look back far enough into Thomas’ career, and you’ll start talking about his football career at Auburn. Here we find ourselves with some conflicting information. Thomas says football coach Pat Dye said he should pursue baseball; Thomas recalls Dye saying, “I think you’ll be a very, very good football player, but you’re not going to be that level that you are in baseball.”</p></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">But Dye now tells the school’s site, “If he had stuck with football, he’d be going in the Hall of Fame as a football player.”</p></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">Either Dye is being polite, or he misspoke and the Sox gained. Either way, Paul Sullivan talked to Mike Rizzo, the scout who signed Thomas. Thomas’ agent tried selling football as an alternate career, and Rizzo didn’t buy it.</p></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><ul class="duet--article--unordered-list _1nfb3k4i feuejx0 ls9zuh1"><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.suntimes.com/sports/baseball/whitesox/28835856-574/obsession-with-stats-helped-push-frank-thomas-to-great-heights.html#.U9RNx0CTG5I">Stats obsession helped push Frank Thomas to great heights - Chicago Sun-Times</a></span></li><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.suntimes.com/sports/baseball/whitesox/28851009-574/paul-konerko-lauds-frank-thomas-for-being-dialed-in-with-his-work.html#.U9RNzECTG5I">Paul Konerko lauds Frank Thomas for being ‘dialed in with his work’ - Chicago Sun-Times</a></span></li></ul></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">Time heals all wounds, not just between Thomas and the Sox, but between Thomas and the people -- media and teammates, mainly -- who thought Thomas paid too much attention to his stats, because they realize that it’s all just motivation. And hell, if my baseball card looked like Thomas’, I’d want to know what my numbers were at all times, too.</p></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><div class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup _458ieq0"><p>Likewise, <a class="sbn-auto-link" href="http://www.sbnation.com/mlb/players/159/paul-konerko">Paul Konerko</a> expresses his admiration for Thomas. Or at least Thomas' preparation.</p></div></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><ul class="duet--article--unordered-list _1nfb3k4i feuejx0 ls9zuh1"><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://hardballtalk.nbcsports.com/2014/07/24/the-eyes-have-it-thomas-greatness-built-on-patience/">Frank Thomas is Hall of Famer because of great batting eye | HardballTalk</a></span></li></ul></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">Joe Posnanski knows that good players’ good stats are good for the team, and so he raves about Thomas’ legendary eye. These two paragraphs are plenty of fun:</p></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><div class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup _458ieq0"><blockquote> <p>In his prime, Thomas was an artist &mdash; more Gwynn than McGwire, more Boggs than Sosa. He would hulk over the plate, and he looked a little bit sleepy up there, and if a pitch was an inch off the plate or an inch below the knee, he would just watch it go by. He knew what pitchers were trying to do. He was like a crocodile: He could stand there perfectly still and convince his prey that he was just a log in the water.</p> <p>And then, when he unleashed, he UNLEASHED &mdash; left foot up in the air then stomp on the ground as he rushed his bat through the strike zone with such force that that the bat seemed to pull his body off the ground. His right leg sometimes came up flying behind him as he followed through. He swung the bat so hard, there did not seem any limit to how far he could hit a baseball. But, many of his best shots were not home runs &mdash; they were screaming line drives that stayed three or four feel off the ground and crashed into the wall so loud you could hear it reverberate through the stadium. <a class="sbn-auto-link" href="http://www.sbnation.com/mlb/players/427/miguel-cabrera">Miguel Cabrera</a> hits baseballs about as hard as Thomas did, but he is so much more balanced. The effect with Thomas was even more awesome because of how much force he put into his swing.</p> </blockquote></div></div><div class="duet--article--block-placement jgpyd51 jgpyd50 duet--article--article-body-component"><ul class="duet--article--unordered-list _1nfb3k4i feuejx0 ls9zuh1"><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://www.chicagotribune.com/sports/baseball/cubs/ct-sullivan-baseball-spt-0727-20140727,0,3472086.story">No place for steroid users in the Hall of Fame - chicagotribune.com</a></span></li><li class="feuejx1"><span class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup"><a href="http://mlb.mlb.com/news/article/cws/big-hurt-stressed-grateful-as-induction-nears?ymd=20140726&content_id=86423432&vkey=news_cws">Big Hurt stressed, grateful as induction nears | whitesox.com: News</a></span></li></ul></div><div class="duet--article--article-body-component"><p class="duet--article--dangerously-set-cms-markup duet--article--standard-paragraph _1nfb3k4i _16w9vov1 _16w9vov0 ls9zuh1">Even if Thomas wanted to spend his Hall of Fame speech lambasting steroid users, it would probably sound redundant after answering all the questions about it over various media sessions dating back to January. Good news -- Thomas said he’s reserving his speech to thank the people along the way who made his career possible. I’m looking forward to seeing it.</p></div><div class="_8kam0j0"><span class="_8kam0j1">See More<!-- -->:<span class="_8kam0j2"> </span></span><ul class="_153sp3of"><li class="_153sp3o0 _153z5vu0"><a href="/chicago-white-sox-news" class="_153sp3o9">Chicago White Sox News</a></li><li class="_153sp3o0 _153z5vu0"><a href="/events" class="_153sp3o9">Events</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div data-concert="medium_rectangle_variable"></div></div></div><div class="_1s30nsr2 _1s30nsr5 _1s30nsr8"><div class="duet--layout--header-pattern _1nfb3k4g _1s30nsr7"><div class="fpbq2w3"><div 2025</div></a><div class="qcdc9h7 qcdc9h6"></div></li><li class="qcdc9h4 qcdc9h3"><a href="/chicago-white-sox-scores-and-standings/116207/the-guardians-hand-the-white-sox-a-second-straight-loss"><div Like we learned in writing about his brief minor-league career, Thomas wasn’t short on confidence, even though -- or because -- he felt like evaluators overlooked him.\n* Cooperstown or Canton for Frank Thomas? - chicagotribune.com\n* Frank Thomas: From Auburn tight end to Cooperstown - AuburnTigers.com\n* Frank Thomas remembers Auburn on way to Hall of Fame - AuburnTigers.com\nLook back far enough into Thomas’ career, and you’ll start talking about his football career at Auburn. Here we find ourselves with some conflicting information. Thomas says football coach Pat Dye said he should pursue baseball; Thomas recalls Dye saying, “I think you’ll be a very, very good football player, but you’re not going to be that level that you are in baseball.”\nBut Dye now tells the school’s site, “If he had stuck with football, he’d be going in the Hall of Fame as a football player.”\nEither Dye is being polite, or he misspoke and the Sox gained. Either way, Paul Sullivan talked to Mike Rizzo, the scout who signed Thomas. Thomas’ agent tried selling football as an alternate career, and Rizzo didn’t buy it.\n* Stats obsession helped push Frank Thomas to great heights - Chicago Sun-Times\n* Paul Konerko lauds Frank Thomas for being ‘dialed in with his work’ - Chicago Sun-Times\nTime heals all wounds, not just between Thomas and the Sox, but between Thomas and the people -- media and teammates, mainly -- who thought Thomas paid too much attention to his stats, because they realize that it’s all just motivation. And hell, if my baseball card looked like Thomas’, I’d want to know what my numbers were at all times, too.\n* Frank Thomas is Hall of Famer because of great batting eye | HardballTalk\nJoe Posnanski knows that good players’ good stats are good for the team, and so he raves about Thomas’ legendary eye. Good news -- Thomas said he’s reserving his speech to thank the people along the way who made his career possible.
